					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American rapper (born 1988)</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the alternative and underground hip hop artist whose career started in the 1990s, see <a href="/wiki/Aesop_Rock" title="Aesop Rock">Aesop Rock</a>.</div>

</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://asaprocky.com">asaprocky<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Rakim Athelaston Mayers</b><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> (born October 3, 1988), known professionally as <b>ASAP Rocky</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;p&#39; in &#39;pie&#39;">p</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">AY</span>-sap</i></a>; stylized as <b>A$AP Rocky</b>), is an American rapper. Born and raised in Harlem, he embarked on his musical career as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> collective <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Mob" title="ASAP Mob">ASAP Mob</a>, from which he adopted his <a href="/wiki/Moniker" class="mw-redirect" title="Moniker">moniker</a>. In August 2011, Rocky's single "<a href="/wiki/Peso_(song)" title="Peso (song)">Peso</a>" was <a href="/wiki/Music_leak" title="Music leak">leaked online</a> and within weeks began receiving radio airplay.<sup id="cite_ref-Caramanica_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caramanica-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Rocky released his debut mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Live._Love._ASAP" title="Live. Love. ASAP">Live. Love. A$AP</a></i>, later that year to widespread critical acclaim. The success of what is considered his breakout project led to a joint venture record deal with <a href="/wiki/Polo_Grounds_Music" title="Polo Grounds Music">Polo Grounds Music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music" title="Sony Music">Sony Music</a>'s <a href="/wiki/RCA_Records" title="RCA Records">RCA Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Coleman_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coleman-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Long._Live._ASAP" title="Long. Live. ASAP">Long. Live. A$AP</a></i> (2013) debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and was later certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">double platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA). The album was preceded by Rocky's breakout single, "<a href="/wiki/Fuckin%27_Problems" title="Fuckin&#39; Problems">Fuckin' Problems</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a>, <a href="/wiki/2_Chainz" title="2 Chainz">2 Chainz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>), which was nominated for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Song" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Song">Best Rap Song</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Grammy Awards">2014 Grammy Awards</a>. In 2015, Rocky released his second album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/At._Long._Last._ASAP" title="At. Long. Last. ASAP">At. Long. Last. A$AP</a></i>. The album was Rocky's second consecutive album to debut at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and received mostly positive reviews from music critics. The album's single, "<a href="/wiki/LSD_(ASAP_Rocky_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="LSD (ASAP Rocky song)">L$D</a>", was nominated for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Music_Video" title="Grammy Award for Best Music Video">Best Music Video</a> at the <a href="/wiki/58th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="58th Annual Grammy Awards">2016 Grammy Awards</a>. In 2018, Rocky released his third album, <i><a href="/wiki/Testing_(album)" title="Testing (album)">Testing</a></i>, which peaked in the top five of several countries, including the <i>Billboard</i> 200.
</p><p>Rocky has won a <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards" title="BET Awards">BET Award</a>, two <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a>, an <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards_Japan" title="MTV Video Music Awards Japan">MTV Video Music Award Japan</a> and an <a href="/wiki/MTVU#MTVU_Woodie_Awards" title="MTVU">MTVU Woodie Award</a>, as well as being nominated for two <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a>, six <a href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards" title="World Music Awards">World Music Awards</a>, three <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Video Music Award">MTV Video Music Awards</a> and two <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Europe Music Award">MTV Europe Music Awards</a>. Rocky has also directed <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music videos</a> for himself, <a href="/wiki/Danny_Brown" title="Danny Brown">Danny Brown</a>, and other A$AP Mob members.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, he produces records under the pseudonym <b>Lord Flacko</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Rakim Athelaston Mayers was born on October 3, 1988, in the <a href="/wiki/Harlem" title="Harlem">Harlem</a> neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, a borough of New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCRocky_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCRocky-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> His father is from <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cooper_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cooper-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> He has an older brother (deceased) and an older sister, Erika.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Both Rakim and Erika's names are taken from the <a href="/wiki/Eric_B._%26_Rakim" title="Eric B. &amp; Rakim">Eric B. &amp; Rakim</a> duo.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitchfork_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitchfork-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> His cousin is fellow <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Mob" title="ASAP Mob">ASAP Mob</a> member <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Nast" title="ASAP Nast">ASAP Nast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mayers started rapping at age nine, when he moved to <a href="/wiki/Harrisburg,_Pennsylvania" title="Harrisburg, Pennsylvania">Harrisburg, Pennsylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He learned how to rap from his older brother, who also wore the <a href="/wiki/Cornrows" title="Cornrows">Cornrows</a> hairdo that A$AP Rocky later adopted. When Mayers was 13, his brother was killed in Harlem.<sup id="cite_ref-Sundermann_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sundermann-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The death inspired Rocky to take rapping more seriously.<sup id="cite_ref-Fader_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fader-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Mayers grew up admiring Harlem-based rap group <a href="/wiki/The_Diplomats" title="The Diplomats">The Diplomats</a>. He was also influenced by <a href="/wiki/Mobb_Deep" title="Mobb Deep">Mobb Deep</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Allmusic_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Three_6_Mafia" title="Three 6 Mafia">Three 6 Mafia</a>, <a href="/wiki/UGK" title="UGK">UGK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Run_DMC" class="mw-redirect" title="Run DMC">Run DMC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wu-Tang_Clan" title="Wu-Tang Clan">Wu-Tang Clan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bone_Thugs-n-Harmony" title="Bone Thugs-n-Harmony">Bone Thugs-n-Harmony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vibe_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vibe-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When Mayers was 12 years old, his father went to jail and he spent his teenage years moving around <a href="/wiki/Homeless_shelter" title="Homeless shelter">homeless shelters</a> with his mother and sister.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> After living for a period in a shelter with his mother in New York City, he moved to <a href="/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan" title="Midtown Manhattan">Midtown Manhattan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> His father died in 2012. <sup id="cite_ref-Maz_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maz-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="2007.E2.80.932011:_Career_beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2007–2011:_Career_beginnings">2007–2011: Career beginnings</span></h3>
<p>In 2007, A$AP Rocky joined the <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Mob" title="ASAP Mob">A$AP Mob</a> crew, a Harlem-based collective of rappers, producers, music video directors, fashion designers, and bikers who shared similar interests in music, fashion, style, and art.<sup id="cite_ref-hypetrak1_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hypetrak1-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> It had been formed by A$AP Yams, A$AP Bari and A$AP Illz.<sup id="cite_ref-vvblogs_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vvblogs-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In July 2011, Rocky released his single "Purple Swag" which quickly became a street anthem in New York City.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In August 2011, Rocky's single "<a href="/wiki/Peso_(song)" title="Peso (song)">Peso</a>", was <a href="/wiki/Music_leak" title="Music leak">leaked online</a> and within weeks received airplay on the high-profile <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">Hot 97</a> New York radio station.<sup id="cite_ref-Caramanica_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caramanica-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> After he released a <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music video</a> for his song "Purple Swag", he received attention from several record labels. In October, he released the mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Live._Love._ASAP" title="Live. Love. ASAP">Live. Love. A$AP</a></i> to critical acclaim. Earlier that month, he signed a two-year, $3 million record deal with Bryan Leach's <a href="/wiki/Polo_Grounds_Music" title="Polo Grounds Music">Polo Grounds Music</a>, which at the time was distributed by <a href="/wiki/Clive_Davis" title="Clive Davis">Clive Davis</a>' <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music" title="Sony Music">Sony Music</a> division of <a href="/wiki/J_Records" title="J Records">J Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Upon his record deal, Rocky started a label, A$AP Worldwide, with A$AP Yams.<sup id="cite_ref-vvblogs_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vvblogs-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> However, Rocky's deal with J Records would be short-lived,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> when on October 7, <a href="/wiki/RCA_Music_Group" title="RCA Music Group">RCA Music Group</a> announced that it was merging J alongside <a href="/wiki/Arista_Records" title="Arista Records">Arista</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jive_Records" title="Jive Records">Jive Records</a> into <a href="/wiki/RCA_Records" title="RCA Records">RCA Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> With the shutdown, Rocky (and all other artists previously signed to these three labels) will release future material under the RCA brand.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> On December 5, he was nominated for <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sound_of..." title="Sound of...">Sound of 2012</a> poll.<sup id="cite_ref-so12_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-so12-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.932014:_Touring_and_Long._Live._A.24AP"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–2014:_Touring_and_Long._Live._A$AP">2012–2014: Touring and <i>Long. Live. A$AP</i></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ASAP_Rocky_Coachella_2012_1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/ASAP_Rocky_Coachella_2012_1.jpg/220px-ASAP_Rocky_Coachella_2012_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/ASAP_Rocky_Coachella_2012_1.jpg/330px-ASAP_Rocky_Coachella_2012_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/ASAP_Rocky_Coachella_2012_1.jpg/440px-ASAP_Rocky_Coachella_2012_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption>ASAP Rocky performing at the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>In February 2012, Rocky joined <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a> as the opening act for <a href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Drake (entertainer)">Drake</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Club_Paradise_Tour" title="Club Paradise Tour">Club Paradise Tour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In June, <a href="/wiki/SpaceGhostPurrp" title="SpaceGhostPurrp">SpaceGhostPurrp</a>, founder of Miami-based collective <a href="/wiki/Raider_Klan" title="Raider Klan">Raider Klan</a> and Rocky's past collaborator, accused A$AP Twelvyy of jumping Raider Klan's Matt Stoops and subsequently disassociated himself from A$AP Mob and Rocky in a YouTube video.<sup id="cite_ref-Markman_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Markman-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> He and Raider Klan also accused ASAP Mob of copying their style,<sup id="cite_ref-Markman_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Markman-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and Rocky of using lyrics from SpaceGhostPurrp's song "My Enemy" on "Goldie".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Rocky responded in a July interview for MTV, saying that SpaceGhostPurrp is "try[ing] to build hype" and told him to "stick to makin' beats".<sup id="cite_ref-Markman_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Markman-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2012, Rocky performed at the <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Music_Festival" title="Pitchfork Music Festival">Pitchfork Music Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lipshutz0714_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lipshutz0714-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He was scheduled to make his network television debut on <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Night_with_Jimmy_Fallon" title="Late Night with Jimmy Fallon">Late Night with Jimmy Fallon</a></i> on July 20,<sup id="cite_ref-Lipshutz0714_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lipshutz0714-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> but he was then arrested the night before, after an alleged involvement in a brawl, with 21-year-old artist iRome. The scuffle took place in downtown Manhattan and the performance was canceled.<sup id="cite_ref-nybrawl2012_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nybrawl2012-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> After it was rescheduled for August 21, Rocky performed "Goldie" on the show.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> On September 6, he also performed a guest rap on <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Cockiness_(Love_It)" title="Cockiness (Love It)">Cockiness (Love It)</a>" at the <a href="/wiki/2012_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2012 MTV Video Music Awards">2012 MTV Video Music Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rocky recorded his debut <a href="/wiki/Studio_album" class="mw-redirect" title="Studio album">studio album</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Long._Live._ASAP" title="Long. Live. ASAP">Long. Live. A$AP</a></i>, along with several producers, such as Clams Casino, Hit-Boy, Friendzone, A$AP Ty Beats, Soufein3000 and Joey Fat Beats.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitzmaurice_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzmaurice-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> "Goldie" was released as the album's first single on April 27.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> On August 27, his crew A$AP Mob released the mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Lords_Never_Worry" title="Lords Never Worry">Lords Never Worry</a></i> as a free download.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> During September through November, Rocky promoted the album with the 40-date national <a href="/wiki/Concert_tour" title="Concert tour">concert tour</a>, the Long Live ASAP Tour, with opening acts <a href="/wiki/Schoolboy_Q" title="Schoolboy Q">ScHoolboy Q</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danny_Brown_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Danny Brown (rapper)">Danny Brown</a>, and A$AP Mob.<sup id="cite_ref-Tour_Information_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tour_Information-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> <i>Long. Live. A$AP</i> was released on January 15, 2013, to mostly positive reviews from critics.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The album debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, with first-week sales of 139,000 copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> As of March&#160;13,&#32;2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=ASAP_Rocky&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, it has sold 284,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> On March 16, 2015, <i>Long. Live. A$AP</i> was certified gold by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA), for the shipment of 500,000 copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 12, 2013, in an interview at <a href="/wiki/Wild_94.9" class="mw-redirect" title="Wild 94.9">Wild 94.9</a> radio station, Rocky revealed that he was working on an <a href="/wiki/Instrumental" title="Instrumental">instrumental</a> album, which he plans on releasing without notice. He even discussed his favorite music videos and talked about his desire to collaborate with veteran rapper <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_3000" title="André 3000">André 3000</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> On June 21, Rocky told <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a> that he had completed his debut instrumental album, which mostly consists of <a href="/wiki/Ambient_music" title="Ambient music">ambient</a> oriented instrumental tracks, titled <i>Beauty &amp; The Beast: Slowed Down Sessions (Chapter 1)</i> and was originally set to be released during the summer for free download.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> However, that album was delayed with no release date announced. Rocky previewed two snippets that would have made the <i>Beauty &amp; The Beast: Slowed Down Sessions (Chapter 1)</i> compilation, titled "Riot Rave" and "Unicorn".<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The project has not been released as of 2022.
</p>
<h3><span id="2015.E2.80.932017:_At._Long._Last._A.24AP"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–2017:_At._Long._Last._A$AP">2015–2017: <i>At. Long. Last. A$AP</i></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ASAP_Rocky_2013.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/ASAP_Rocky_2013.jpg/220px-ASAP_Rocky_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/ASAP_Rocky_2013.jpg/330px-ASAP_Rocky_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/ASAP_Rocky_2013.jpg/440px-ASAP_Rocky_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667" /></a><figcaption>ASAP Rocky in 2013</figcaption></figure>
<p>On March 16, 2014, Rocky announced that he was working on his second studio album, entitled <i>A.L.L.A.</i> (an acronym for <i><a href="/wiki/At._Long._Last._ASAP" title="At. Long. Last. ASAP">At. Long. Last. A$AP</a></i>)<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> which was a follow-up to his debut album, <i>Long. Live. A$AP</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Upon the wake of a delay of the <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Mob" title="ASAP Mob">ASAP Mob</a> album, <i>L.O.R.D.</i>, Rocky subsequently collaborated with cohorts <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Ferg" title="ASAP Ferg">A$AP Ferg</a>, Nast and Twelvyy on the album's third single, "Hella Hoes", which was released on June 6, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, A$AP Mob leader A$AP Yams announced on his <a href="/wiki/Tumblr" title="Tumblr">Tumblr</a> account that the album had been shelved.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 3, 2014, his 26th birthday, Rocky launched a short-lived music giveaway called Flacko Jodye Season,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> which first premiered with "<a href="/wiki/Multiply_(ASAP_Rocky_song)" title="Multiply (ASAP Rocky song)">Multiply</a>", which featured additional vocals from <a href="/wiki/Juicy_J" title="Juicy J">Juicy J</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-soundcloud_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soundcloud-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-billboard_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> later released on iTunes one week after its premiere.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year&#39;s Day">New Year's Day 2015</a>, Rocky released his second album's <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Lord_Pretty_Flacko_Jodye_2_(LPFJ2)" title="Lord Pretty Flacko Jodye 2 (LPFJ2)">Lord Pretty Flacko Jodye 2 (LPFJ2)</a>", a sequel to "Pretty Flacko".<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Then, on January 18, seventeen days after the single's release, Rocky's mentor and partner, Steven "A$AP Yams" Rodriguez, died at the age of 26.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BET_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BET-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> However, some reports later stated that Yams' cause was ruled acute mixed drug intoxication<sup id="cite_ref-yams_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yams-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> while Rocky and several A$AP Mob members and affiliates said that the late leader of the collective died due to his <a href="/wiki/Sleep_apnea" title="Sleep apnea">sleep apnea</a>, which caused <a href="/wiki/Asphyxiation" class="mw-redirect" title="Asphyxiation">asphyxiation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_aspiration" title="Pulmonary aspiration">pulmonary aspiration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Weeks after Yams' death, Rocky revealed that <i>At. Long. Last. A$AP</i> was executive-produced by rapper <a href="/wiki/Juicy_J" title="Juicy J">Juicy J</a>, producer <a href="/wiki/Danger_Mouse_(musician)" title="Danger Mouse (musician)">Danger Mouse</a>, Rocky and Yams themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hypebeast_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hypebeast-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, Rocky appeared in a cameo role in the <a href="/wiki/Indie_film" class="mw-redirect" title="Indie film">indie</a> comedy-drama, <i><a href="/wiki/Dope_(2015_film)" title="Dope (2015 film)">Dope</a></i>. The film premiered at the <a href="/wiki/2015_Sundance_Film_Festival" title="2015 Sundance Film Festival">2015 Sundance Film Festival</a> on January 21, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> It opened in all movie theaters on June 12.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> There at the event, Rocky explained his expressions and grief over the death of his own friend and partner; performed "Multiply" on-stage as a dedication to his loving memory, minutes before running backstage to calm down.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2015, Rocky said in an interview with <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a> that he made songs such as "Wild For The Night" and "Fuckin' Problems" for mainstream commercial success, and that he now hated those songs.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 8, 2015, the rapper released a song, titled "<a href="/wiki/M%27s_(song)" title="M&#39;s (song)">M'$</a>", debuted during an interview with the <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Music_Academy" title="Red Bull Music Academy">Red Bull Music Academy</a>, and was released on the <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a> two days later,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> however, it was announced that the song was not an official single from the album.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The album, however, did include a remixed version of the track that replaced Rocky's second verse with a guest verse from <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>. On May 9, Rocky unveiled the album's <a href="/wiki/Cover_art" title="Cover art">cover art</a> on his official <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> page, with the caption "AT LONG LAST...."<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> On the same day, he then released the album's alternative artwork<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> and released the album's second single, titled "<a href="/wiki/Everyday_(ASAP_Rocky_song)" title="Everyday (ASAP Rocky song)">Everyday</a>" featuring <a href="/wiki/Rod_Stewart" title="Rod Stewart">Rod Stewart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_(singer)" title="Miguel (singer)">Miguel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ronson" title="Mark Ronson">Mark Ronson</a> (the latter of which also produced the track alongside <a href="/wiki/Emile_Haynie" title="Emile Haynie">Emile Haynie</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-facebook.com_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facebook.com-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Rocky also announced that the release date for <i>A.L.L.A.</i> was updated to June 2, 2015; however, on May 25, 2015, around 6:00 PM EDT, the album <a href="/wiki/Music_leak" title="Music leak">leaked online</a>, approximately one week before its expected release.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently, Rocky tweeted to announce that the album will be released at midnight (May 26), changing the date a week early.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Upon its release, <i>At. Long. Last. A$AP</i> received generally positive to mixed reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_critics" class="mw-redirect" title="Music critics">music critics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Overall, the album was supported by the release of three <a href="/wiki/Single_(music)" title="Single (music)">singles</a>: "<a href="/wiki/Lord_Pretty_Flacko_Jodye_2_(LPFJ2)" title="Lord Pretty Flacko Jodye 2 (LPFJ2)">Lord Pretty Flacko Jodye 2 (LPFJ2)</a>", "Everyday" and "<a href="/wiki/LSD_(ASAP_Rocky_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="LSD (ASAP Rocky song)">L$D</a>". <i>At. Long. Last. A$AP</i> debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, selling 116,000 copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In conclusion to this, it also gave Rocky his second consecutive number one album on the charts to date.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> In Canada, the album debuted at number one, with 11,000 copies sold.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The album has spent two more weeks beyond the top ten of the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> As of July&#160;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=ASAP_Rocky&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the album has sold 215,000 copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> It has sold 60,662 copies in the United Kingdom, as of June&#160;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=ASAP_Rocky&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> However, despite being his second consecutive number-one album, <i>At. Long. Last. ASAP</i> began to decline in album-equivalent sales, becoming Rocky's lowest-selling album in his career.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>On June 11, 2015, Rocky was featured on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_Starring_Jimmy_Fallon" title="The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon">The Tonight Show</a></i>, where he performed the song "L$D" with <a href="/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">The Roots</a>. In June, it was confirmed that he was featured on the single "<a href="/wiki/Good_for_You_(song)" title="Good for You (song)">Good for You</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez" title="Selena Gomez">Selena Gomez</a>. In June 2015, he appeared on the "Carpool Karaoke" segment of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Late_Late_Show_with_James_Corden" title="The Late Late Show with James Corden">The Late Late Show</a></i>, riding with Rod Stewart and host <a href="/wiki/James_Corden" title="James Corden">James Corden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rocky is featured on "<a href="/wiki/Blended_Family_(What_You_Do_for_Love)" title="Blended Family (What You Do for Love)">Blended Family (What You Do for Love)</a>", a track written with <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a> for her sixth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Here_(Alicia_Keys_album)" title="Here (Alicia Keys album)">Here</a></i> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> He is also featured on two tracks from the 2017 album <i><a href="/wiki/Lust_for_Life_(Lana_Del_Rey_album)" title="Lust for Life (Lana Del Rey album)">Lust for Life</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Lana_Del_Rey" title="Lana Del Rey">Lana Del Rey</a>. The tracks are called "Summer Bummer", which also features <a href="/wiki/Playboi_Carti" title="Playboi Carti">Playboi Carti</a>, and "Groupie Love".<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> He also featured in "<a href="/wiki/Pick_It_Up_(Famous_Dex_song)" title="Pick It Up (Famous Dex song)">Pick It Up</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Famous_Dex" title="Famous Dex">Famous Dex</a>, released in October 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2018.E2.80.93present:_Testing_and_upcoming_fourth_studio_album"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–present:_Testing_and_upcoming_fourth_studio_album">2018–present: <i>Testing</i> and upcoming fourth studio album</span></h3>
<p>On January 23, 2018, ASAP Rocky released "☆☆☆☆☆ 5ive $tar$" on <a href="/wiki/SoundCloud" title="SoundCloud">SoundCloud</a>, produced by <a href="/wiki/Metro_Boomin" title="Metro Boomin">Metro Boomin</a>, Frans Mernick, Jordan Blackmon and Daniel Lynas and featuring uncredited vocals by <a href="/wiki/DRAM_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="DRAM (rapper)">DRAM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Over the following two days he shared "Above", produced by Mernick and "Money Bags Freestyle (<a href="/wiki/Dean_Blunt" title="Dean Blunt">Dean Blunt</a> Meditation)", produced by Blunt and featuring uncredited vocals by <a href="/wiki/Lil_Yachty" title="Lil Yachty">Lil Yachty</a>. The songs were captioned "TESTING COMING SOON" and "THIS IS JUST A TEST", leading to speculation that they were in promotion of an upcoming studio album entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Testing_(album)" title="Testing (album)">Testing</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> On February 16, Rocky collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Gucci_Mane" title="Gucci Mane">Gucci Mane</a> and <a href="/wiki/21_Savage" title="21 Savage">21 Savage</a> for "Cocky", in promotion of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Uncle_Drew_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Uncle Drew (film)">Uncle Drew</a></i>. He released the single "Bad Company" on March 27. It features rapper <a href="/wiki/BlocBoy_JB" title="BlocBoy JB">BlocBoy JB</a>, as well as further allusions to <i>Testing</i> in its marketing.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> On April 5, he released a second single: "ASAP Forever". The song samples record producer <a href="/wiki/Moby" title="Moby">Moby</a>'s 2000 single "<a href="/wiki/Porcelain_(song)" title="Porcelain (song)">Porcelain</a>", crediting him as a featured artist. It was premiered on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show" title="The Tonight Show">The Tonight Show</a></i> alongside new track "Distorted Records", and a music video was released the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> A day later he was featured on the song "One Track Mind", from rock band <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Seconds_to_Mars" title="Thirty Seconds to Mars">Thirty Seconds to Mars</a>' fifth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/America_(Thirty_Seconds_to_Mars_album)" title="America (Thirty Seconds to Mars album)">America</a></i>.
</p><p>On May 25, 2018, Rocky released <i>Testing</i> to generally positive reviews from critics. It debuted at number four on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, becoming ASAP Rocky's third consecutive top-five album on the chart, but another low-seller.<sup id="cite_ref-HipHopDX1_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HipHopDX1-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_200_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_200-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> In its second week, the album dropped to number 15, with 26,000 album-equivalent units (1,000 copies).<sup id="cite_ref-HipHopDX2_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HipHopDX2-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The following week, <i>Testing</i> dropped to number 22 on the chart.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_200_Week_3_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_200_Week_3-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> On July 23, 2018, Rocky and <a href="/wiki/Tyler,_the_Creator" title="Tyler, the Creator">Tyler, The Creator</a> announced a collaborative project, <i>WANGSAP</i>, by releasing a music video of a remix of <a href="/wiki/Monica_(singer)" title="Monica (singer)">Monica's</a> "<a href="/wiki/Knock_Knock_(Monica_song)" title="Knock Knock (Monica song)">Knock Knock</a>" named "Potato Salad" on AWGE's "AWGE DVD (Vol. 3)".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> However, on January 23, 2019, Tyler, the Creator announced this album never existed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In May 2019, Juicy J announced Rocky began working on his upcoming album, formerly titled <i>All Smiles</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> On August 28, ASAP Rocky released the music video for "<a href="/wiki/Babushka_Boi" title="Babushka Boi">Babushka Boi</a>". It was directed by Nadia Lee Cohen.
</p><p>In October 2021, ASAP Rocky released his 2011 mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Live._Love._ASAP" title="Live. Love. ASAP">Live. Love. ASAP</a></i> to all streaming platforms in celebration of its 10-year anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rocky appeared on two tracks from <a href="/wiki/Nigo" title="Nigo">Nigo</a>'s album, <i>I Know Nigo!</i>, released March 25, 2022, the opening track "Lost and Found Freestyle 2019" with <a href="/wiki/Tyler,_the_Creator" title="Tyler, the Creator">Tyler, the Creator</a>, and the single, "Arya".<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Rocky supported the <a href="/wiki/Red_Hot_Chili_Peppers" title="Red Hot Chili Peppers">Red Hot Chili Peppers</a> on their <a href="/wiki/Red_Hot_Chili_Peppers_2022_Global_Stadium_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Hot Chili Peppers 2022 Global Stadium Tour">2022 international stadium tour</a>. After he arrived late for a performance at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>, Manchester, he performed a shortened 20-minute set after the Chili Peppers.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2022, Rocky released the single, "D.M.B.",<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> and followed up in December with "Shittin' Me".<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Also in December, he appeared on producer Metro Boomin's album <i><a href="/wiki/Heroes_%26_Villains" title="Heroes &amp; Villains">Heroes &amp; Villains</a></i>, on the track "Feel the Fiyaaaah", which also featured late rapper <a href="/wiki/Takeoff_(rapper)" title="Takeoff (rapper)">Takeoff</a>, who was gunned down a month prior to the album's release.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> He then confirmed a new album with production from Metro Boomin to materalize in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, he named his upcoming fourth album, <i>Don't Be Dumb</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_ventures">Business ventures</span></h2>
<p>In October 2011, Rocky signed a record deal with <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Sony Music Entertainment">Sony Music Entertainment</a> worth $3 million ($1.7 million of which was earmarked for his solo work; $1.3 million earmarked to fund his company).<sup id="cite_ref-Adaso_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adaso-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Rocky said that he sought a "bigger platform" for him and his collective with the deal.<sup id="cite_ref-Coleman_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coleman-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> His first studio album planned to be under the deal, but it allowed him to continue releasing mixtapes through <a href="/wiki/RED_Associated_Labels" class="mw-redirect" title="RED Associated Labels">Sony/RED</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Coleman_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coleman-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Fellow rapper and A$AP Mob member <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Ferg" title="ASAP Ferg">A$AP Ferg</a> also signed a joint venture deal with the RCA-distributed Polo Grounds Music; Ferg released his single "Work", for digital retail via various platforms. He later announced an official <a href="/wiki/Remix" title="Remix">remix</a> featuring Rocky, <a href="/wiki/French_Montana" title="French Montana">French Montana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schoolboy_Q" title="Schoolboy Q">ScHoolboy Q</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_James" title="Trinidad James">Trinidad James</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, he and ASAP Mob co-founder <a href="/wiki/ASAP_Bari" title="ASAP Bari">ASAP Bari</a><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> released his A$AP merchandise brand, and went to collaborate with high-profile fashion designer and close friend <a href="/wiki/Raf_Simons" title="Raf Simons">Raf Simons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> On October 2, 2014, A$AP Rocky announced he had officially signed a contract for worldwide representation with <a href="/wiki/William_Morris_Endeavor" class="mw-redirect" title="William Morris Endeavor">William Morris Endeavor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mtv.com_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtv.com-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2016, <a href="/wiki/Guess_(clothing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Guess (clothing)">Guess</a> released a collaboration with Rocky called GUE$$, which was inspired by Rocky's admiration for the brand's vintage '90s clothing that he wore while growing up.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>From 2011 to 2012, Rocky dated Australian rapper <a href="/wiki/Iggy_Azalea" title="Iggy Azalea">Iggy Azalea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> He began dating model <a href="/wiki/Chanel_Iman" title="Chanel Iman">Chanel Iman</a> in early 2013, and in April 2014, they were reported to be engaged,<sup id="cite_ref-people140407_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-people140407-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> but broke up in June 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 19, 2021, Rocky revealed during an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a></i> that he is in a relationship with Barbadian singer <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>, describing her as "the love of my life".<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The two were first linked in 2013, after Rocky opened up for Rihanna's <a href="/wiki/Diamonds_World_Tour" title="Diamonds World Tour">Diamonds World Tour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> On January 31, 2022, <i><a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)">People</a></i> reported that the couple is expecting their first child.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> On May 19, 2022, it was confirmed that Rihanna had given birth to a boy.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LVII_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl LVII halftime show">Super Bowl LVII halftime show</a>, Rihanna revealed that she was pregnant with the couple's second child.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rocky was a <a href="/wiki/Pescetarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Pescetarian">pescetarian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, he transitioned to a <a href="/wiki/Vegetarianism" title="Vegetarianism">vegetarian</a> diet with the help of his vegan manager after learning of the horrors of the poultry industry.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> On his 2019 single "Babushka Boi", Rocky stated he is now a <a href="/wiki/Veganism" title="Veganism">vegan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rocky has said that while he was raised in a Christian household, he does not like going to an organized church, and instead has "[his] own relationship with God... I pray every day before I go to sleep."<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> He addresses these views in the song "Holy Ghost" on his 2015 album <i><a href="/wiki/At._Long._Last._ASAP" title="At. Long. Last. ASAP">At. Long. Last. ASAP</a></i>. During Rocky's 2019 incarceration in Sweden, he prayed to keep himself occupied.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span></h2>
<p>In 2006, A$AP Rocky served two weeks in <a href="/wiki/Rikers_Island" title="Rikers Island">Rikers Island</a> for drug dealing, where he shared a cell with future rapper <a href="/wiki/Casanova_(rapper)" title="Casanova (rapper)">Casanova</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Breakfast_Club_Power_105.1_FM_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Breakfast_Club_Power_105.1_FM-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 19, 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-Lipshutz0714_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lipshutz0714-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> he was arrested after his alleged participation in a brawl that took place in downtown Manhattan that involved a 21-year-old artist named iRome.<sup id="cite_ref-nybrawl2012_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nybrawl2012-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2012, he was sued by Shenick Alcine who reported that he was assaulted by A$AP Rocky after Alcine observed the rapper doing illegal drugs in a clothing store in New York. He was later arrested for assaulting two amateur photographers who took photos of the incident. That incident ended with a plea bargain where he pled guilty to grand larceny for trying to take their cameras.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 31, 2013, A$AP Rocky allegedly slapped a woman during the <a href="/wiki/Budweiser" title="Budweiser">Budweiser</a> <a href="/wiki/Made_in_America_Festival" title="Made in America Festival">Made in America Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, Pennsylvania. He was charged "with misdemeanor simple assault, a class two misdemeanor". The case was dismissed after a witness failed to appear in court.<sup id="cite_ref-RSslap_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RSslap-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The woman later filed a lawsuit in July 2014, asserting that she still suffered certain conditions as a consequence of the alleged assault.<sup id="cite_ref-RSslap_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RSslap-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> A$AP Rocky stated that he never touched the woman in question and that she "should have known that there could be trouble in place with so many people".<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The lawsuit was settled between the two in April 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In late-September 2015, Rocky was sued by his former manager, Geno Sims, for an alleged breach of agreement, prompting him to countersue.<sup id="cite_ref-yahoo.com_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo.com-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> The lawsuit sought $300,000 in damages.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Four years later, in 2019, Rocky and Sims reached a legal agreement, dropping both suits against one another.<sup id="cite_ref-yahoo.com_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo.com-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Assault_in_Sweden">Assault in Sweden</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:MaxH%C3%B6torget.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/MaxH%C3%B6torget.jpg/220px-MaxH%C3%B6torget.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/MaxH%C3%B6torget.jpg/330px-MaxH%C3%B6torget.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/MaxH%C3%B6torget.jpg/440px-MaxH%C3%B6torget.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Max_Hamburgers" title="Max Hamburgers">Max Hamburgers</a> at <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B6torget" title="Hötorget">Hötorget</a> where the first contact was made. The victim's headphones were retrieved from the awning on the left in the picture.</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ApelbergsgatanStockholm.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/ApelbergsgatanStockholm.jpg/220px-ApelbergsgatanStockholm.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="331" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/ApelbergsgatanStockholm.jpg/330px-ApelbergsgatanStockholm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/ApelbergsgatanStockholm.jpg/440px-ApelbergsgatanStockholm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4288" /></a><figcaption>Apelbergsgatan behind Max Burgers where the final assault took place</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ASAP_Rocky_in_court_in_Sweden.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ASAP_Rocky_in_court_in_Sweden.jpg/220px-ASAP_Rocky_in_court_in_Sweden.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ASAP_Rocky_in_court_in_Sweden.jpg/330px-ASAP_Rocky_in_court_in_Sweden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ASAP_Rocky_in_court_in_Sweden.jpg/440px-ASAP_Rocky_in_court_in_Sweden.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5865" data-file-height="3872" /></a><figcaption>Media and audience outside <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_District_Court" title="Stockholm District Court">Stockholm District Court</a> where the trial against ASAP Rocky was being held</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Don%27t_free_A$AP_Rocky.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="Street art saying Free A$AP Rocky, with the addition Don&#39;t in front." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Don%27t_free_A%24AP_Rocky.jpg/220px-Don%27t_free_A%24AP_Rocky.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Don%27t_free_A%24AP_Rocky.jpg/330px-Don%27t_free_A%24AP_Rocky.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Don%27t_free_A%24AP_Rocky.jpg/440px-Don%27t_free_A%24AP_Rocky.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3024" data-file-height="4032" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Graffiti" title="Graffiti">Graffiti</a> about A$AP Rocky in Stockholm</figcaption></figure>
<p>In July 2019, A$AP Rocky was arrested initially for <a href="/wiki/Aggravated_assault" class="mw-redirect" title="Aggravated assault">aggravated</a>, then for simple <a href="/wiki/Assault" title="Assault">assault</a> in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, after an altercation in the street against a man named Mustafa Jafari and another person that involved A$AP Rocky and three of his entourage on June 30.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Jafari was beaten, kicked, and cut with broken bottles when down on the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> He suffered several cuts, requiring stitches, and a fractured rib.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> A$AP Rocky uploaded two videos of the incident to <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a>. In the first, he and his entourage repeatedly ask two young men, including Jafari, to stop following them as the latter complains about his headphones.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> In the other, created from footage of assorted events, Jafari's headphones break during a scuffle, and he is seen hitting A$AP Rocky's bodyguard with them. A woman is also seen in the video, accusing the two men of <a href="/wiki/Groping" title="Groping">groping</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Henrik Olsson Lilja, the defense attorney for A$AP Rocky, maintained that his client acted in self-defense after being attacked by Jafari.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A$AP Rocky's bodyguard filed a counter-complaint against Jafari,<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> and Jafari was initially suspected of harassment and minor assault or possibly attempted assault.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The investigation against Jafari was dropped as prosecutors said he acted in self-defense, after being grabbed by the neck and pushed by the bodyguard.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> A$AP Rocky was arrested after being allowed to finish his gig at Stadion.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> As it was judged there was a risk that he may flee or tamper with evidence, he was kept in custody at <a href="/wiki/Kronobergsh%C3%A4ktet" title="Kronobergshäktet">Kronoberg Remand Prison</a> until the trial,<sup id="cite_ref-DNdetainonsuspicion_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DNdetainonsuspicion-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> with two members of his entourage also under arrest.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> A$AP Rocky's ongoing tour was then put on hiatus due to the trial.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He was visited by personnel from the US embassy shortly after his arrest.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Several US artists called for a boycott of Sweden due to the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> A petition to release him was started.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The family asked <a href="/wiki/Al_Sharpton" title="Al Sharpton">Al Sharpton</a> for help.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">US President</a> <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> tweeted his support for Rocky, and it was later revealed by justice minister <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Johansson" title="Morgan Johansson">Morgan Johansson</a> that Trump had threatened trade restrictions against Sweden if Rocky was not released.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Former US ambassador to Sweden <a href="/wiki/Mark_Brzezinski" title="Mark Brzezinski">Mark Brzezinski</a> suggested that the government should intervene and speculated that racism may have been the cause of the brawl.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Margot_Wallstr%C3%B6m" title="Margot Wallström">Margot Wallström</a> said the government is not allowed to interfere citing Chapter 11 §3 of the Swedish constitutional <a href="/wiki/Basic_Laws_of_Sweden#Instrument_of_Government" title="Basic Laws of Sweden">Instrument of Government</a> which explicitly forbids the interference of politicians, or unrelated government offices, in the work of the courts of law.
</p><p>A$AP Rocky was convicted of assault, given a <a href="/wiki/Suspended_sentence" title="Suspended sentence">suspended prison sentence</a> and asked to pay 12,500 kr ($1,270) in <a href="/wiki/Damages" title="Damages">damages</a> to the victim.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The court could not decide who used the bottle, but said it was not a case of self-defense.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> As A$AP Rocky had already served over a month in jail for the incident before the sentence was handed out, it was determined that he did not need to serve any additional time.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> The conviction does not bar him from returning to Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alleged_assault_in_Hollywood">Alleged assault in Hollywood</span></h3>
<p>On April 20, 2022, A$AP Rocky was arrested by <a href="/wiki/LAPD" class="mw-redirect" title="LAPD">LAPD</a> officers upon arriving to the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles International Airport</a> after a vacation with his partner, Rihanna. He was arrested for a potential assault with a deadly weapon in a Hollywood shooting on November 6, 2021. Bail was set at $550,000 and he was released shortly after.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After his arrest, detectives executed a warrant to search his home, gaining entry by using a pry bar to force the gate open. Detectives took several boxes from his home to use as evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> On August 15, 2022, the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County_District_Attorney" title="Los Angeles County District Attorney">Los Angeles County District Attorney</a>'s office filed charges against Rocky.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accomplishments">Accomplishments</span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_ASAP_Rocky" title="List of awards and nominations received by ASAP Rocky">List of awards and nominations received by ASAP Rocky</a></div>
<p>His <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_ASAP_Rocky" title="List of awards and nominations received by ASAP Rocky">accomplishments</a> include three <a href="/wiki/BET_Awards" title="BET Awards">BET Awards</a>, two <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="MTV Video Music Awards">awards</a>, and nominations for two <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a> and six <a href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards" title="World Music Awards">World Music Awards</a>, for a total of five wins and 37 nominations overall.
</p>
